  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_69e9c230-97bf-4364-89a9-42d0a6edad69'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_181634547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181634547" />
    <a title="Whitlea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5538129-whitlea"><img alt="Whitlea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309658467p2/5538129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181634547?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitlea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitlea" href="/user/show/5538129-whitlea">Whitlea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5538129-whitlea?shelf=didn-t-like">didn-t-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181634547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9266539141876529977">I was really surprised that I didn't like this one. I had enjoyed what I had read of Lasky's Ga'hoole series, and I was expecting this to be comparable in quality to that. <br/><br/>There were two main issues I had with this book. The first one is that it is horribly dull. The beginning was very exciting, but the first two parts were uninteresting. It didn't help that the main character doesn't have that much of a personality. It started to pick up around the end, but it was too little too late for me. <br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9266539141876529977" style="display:none">I was really surprised that I didn't like this one. I had enjoyed what I had read of Lasky's Ga'hoole series, and I was expecting this to be comparable in quality to that. <br /><br />There were two main issues I had with this book. The first one is that it is horribly dull. The beginning was very exciting, but the first two parts were uninteresting. It didn't help that the main character doesn't have that much of a personality. It started to pick up around the end, but it was too little too late for me. <br /><br />The other issue I have is that the way the society of wolves was portrayed. It irked me to no end that Clans of wolves were considered "noble" as opposed to the cannibals living on the outskirts. Killing innocent wolf pups in the name of genetic purity is on the same level as killing one of your own to eat, in my opinion. I was expecting somewhat of a challenge to be made against their highly unethical practices. I would have liked this book a whole lot better if we had at least been given that. <br /><br />I suppose this might be corrected future installments, but why bother? This promised to be an exciting animal fantasy, but instead I found myself bored and irritated beyond belief by the end of the novel. Honestly, I'd recommend skipping this one and picking up something like Guardians of Ga'hoole or Warriors instead. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9266539141876529977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I am so glad I read it, it was a really well told story of a wolf named Faolan who was born "malcadh" which meant he had some type of disability which in his case was a splayed paw with a swirl on the bottom pad. Malcadh pups are taken away and left to die to keep the packs strong and healthy. Faolan was rescued by a grizzly bear named Thunderheart who had just lost a cub and she became his milk mother. This story brought out so many emotions and the characters felt so real to me. I can't wait to read the next book in the series.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251892324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13758171846856987212">This book frustrated me. I loved Laskey's past series on owls so it could only be assumed that this book would be similar but with wolves. However, it wasn't. <br/><br/>A few of my problems included - <br/><br/>-This book was a lot of "tell" not show. There were pages of descriptions, describing wolf packs, habits, personality, behaviors. There isn't a lot of character interaction, and it almost feels like I'm reading a textbook. The author picks up conversations in the last 30 pages or so but by then it lost me. <br/><br/>-</span>
  <span id="freeText13758171846856987212" style="display:none">This book frustrated me. I loved Laskey's past series on owls so it could only be assumed that this book would be similar but with wolves. However, it wasn't. <br /><br />A few of my problems included - <br /><br />-This book was a lot of "tell" not show. There were pages of descriptions, describing wolf packs, habits, personality, behaviors. There isn't a lot of character interaction, and it almost feels like I'm reading a textbook. The author picks up conversations in the last 30 pages or so but by then it lost me. <br /><br />-The owls. I understand that the Beyond is close to the previous series of books with the owls, but it seemed the reader was contantly being drilled that the owls were close and that YES this author was the author of the Owl series. It's like this series couldn't stand alone without the random owl comparison, or sentence. <br /><br />-The main character is dull. Not because there isn't a personality but because one isn't developed. This has to go with the whole "telling" not showing. So by the time the main character developed I knew nothing about them. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13758171846856987212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421916544?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Trent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Trent" href="/user/show/12832303-chelsea-trent">Chelsea Trent</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421916544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084029698656600679">This book is of a series of 4 books with the mystifying adventures of a young wolf pup named Foalan. I am currently reading the 2nd book: Watch Wolf. Growing up i've had an undying passion for wolves, i raised two wolf pups, Megan and Shiba, of which I found as orphans and decided to adopt them. My friend recommended this book to me as she noticed i am obsessed with wolves. This book tells of a wolf pup who was exiled from his pack due to being "diffirent" Seperated from his pack and parents, he</span>
  <span id="freeText18084029698656600679" style="display:none">This book is of a series of 4 books with the mystifying adventures of a young wolf pup named Foalan. I am currently reading the 2nd book: Watch Wolf. Growing up i've had an undying passion for wolves, i raised two wolf pups, Megan and Shiba, of which I found as orphans and decided to adopt them. My friend recommended this book to me as she noticed i am obsessed with wolves. This book tells of a wolf pup who was exiled from his pack due to being "diffirent" Seperated from his pack and parents, he was left to die, literally. In pack law if there is a deformity in a pup, the pup is taken someplace where death is certain and the mother is banned from the pack and forbidden from returning so that the packs bloodline is not corrupted. I don't want to spoil this book so i'll only tell you my favorite part, when Foalon is left to die by the Obea, he ends up washing up on shore before a grizzly mother overtaken by grief and ready to throw her life away. The grizzly had lost her two cubs to a male grizzly who ruthlessly killed them for a chance to mate with her, when she finds Foalon she thinks of him as a gift from the heavens and a reason for living. This is my favorite part because, without eachother they both would've died. This book is a great stress reliever and a book to get your creative juices flowing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18084029698656600679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323702264" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9311282698659241269">(Written by my ten-year-old daughter as part of a Language Arts assignment)<br/><br/>The Wolves of the Beyond, The Lone Wolf, by Kathryn Lasky is a thrilling novel about a wolf pup named Faolan as he embarks on the journey of a lifetime. This book has enticed many readers and will leave you hunting for more as you learn of a destiny written in the stars...<br/><br/>When a she-wolf named Moragg gives birth to a pup with a splayed paw, she knows the rules of her clan force her to leave him to die. But when Thunderhea</span>
  <span id="freeText9311282698659241269" style="display:none">(Written by my ten-year-old daughter as part of a Language Arts assignment)<br /><br />The Wolves of the Beyond, The Lone Wolf, by Kathryn Lasky is a thrilling novel about a wolf pup named Faolan as he embarks on the journey of a lifetime. This book has enticed many readers and will leave you hunting for more as you learn of a destiny written in the stars...<br /><br />When a she-wolf named Moragg gives birth to a pup with a splayed paw, she knows the rules of her clan force her to leave him to die. But when Thunderheart the bear rescues him and named him Faolan, the pair become inseparable. When tragedy hits, Faolan must strike out on his own in a world full of danger.<br /><br />This enchanting read will unveil your inner fangirl with a character we can all relate to. It teaches a lesson many fail to teach, the social crime of prejudice and how not to judge someone by what you see, but by their heart.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_239991286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239991286" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7036713-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573677691p2/7036713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239991286?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/7036713-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239991286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer988954402902237353">I want to start off by saying that I generally love Kathryn Lasky's books- I read all but a couple of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole series and all of her additions to the Royal Diaries series and thought they were fantastic. This book however was surprisingly dull. I wanted so much to like this book and, it being a kind of "kid's book" thought I would finish it in about a day when it actually took me about 3-4 days. I had to force myself to pick it up and slog through it- working diligently just to </span>
  <span id="freeText988954402902237353" style="display:none">I want to start off by saying that I generally love Kathryn Lasky's books- I read all but a couple of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole series and all of her additions to the Royal Diaries series and thought they were fantastic. This book however was surprisingly dull. I wanted so much to like this book and, it being a kind of "kid's book" thought I would finish it in about a day when it actually took me about 3-4 days. I had to force myself to pick it up and slog through it- working diligently just to make it from chapter to chapter because I really hate to not finish a book and I was in a hurry to start The Giver, which was recommended by my boyfriend.<br /><br />In the Guardians series, Lasky does a very good job of explaining things like twixt time and yeep in the context of the story without distracting from the plot and characters. Explanations in this book however seemed to stand out like ugly sores, distracting and obvious in the worst way. Things are also explained that the main character doesn't even understand like the name for the spirit of a pack running together. The explanation for what I will call the magical cave is somehow both extremely lengthy and dull while also very uninformative. I'm still not quite sure what it was- were the pictures moving? did he literally hear animals? how was he "reading" the images? did time literally stop for him? etc., etc., etc. Yet the discussion of this magical cave spans a ridiculous amount of pages and is mentioned several times afterward. <br /><br />Even without lengthy and very numerous explanations, the book just doesn't flow. Faolan goes from event to event with nothing to really tie them together. The whole story is a little preposterous as well in so many various ways: Faolan is like a super wolf and unless there is a plot twist that reveals the true reason, the only explanation is that his bear mother pushed him to be more physical; The animals seem to be able to spot constellations with almost disgusting ease and see spirits literally traveling through the sky and recognize each one; this wolf manages to bring down a cougar and a full grown caribou (albeit an old one) alone- say what?; the wolf chiefs wore headdresses, necklaces, and ceremonial robes- who made those things?? the canines with no opposable thumbs??<br /><br />I noticed as I was reading that my interest was piqued only when the rogue smith owl was introduced and thought maybe I would begin to like it, but as the perspective shifted back to the main character, I realized it was the just the part of me that loved the Guardians- not that I had actually begun to like this book. I read this on my kindle so I don't have a page count but honestly it isn't necessary. I only became slightly interested after part 3 started and only really liked the final chapter. The last chapter is seriously the only time when there is semblance of action and even that is very anti-climactic. This probably isn't enough to convince me to read/ pay for the next book since I'm too scared I'll be forced to wade through more pages of uninteresting character "development", unimportant observations, and lengthy explanations of every aspect of their world.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this book, especially since I paid for it on my kindle while most books I had downloaded were free and because I liked Lasky's work so much, but the only saving grace for Lone Wolf were things taken straight out of her other novels and the last chapter. I would never recommend this book to anyone- especially wolf lovers. I would steer them gently in the direction of the Guardians series if they wanted an interesting and exciting novel about an almost mythical realm of anthropomorphic animals with their own ways and customs, which is what I felt this book promised to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="988954402902237353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_236626063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236626063" />
    <a title="TeaDrinkingCat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4965293-teadrinkingcat"><img alt="TeaDrinkingCat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444189287p2/4965293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236626063?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TeaDrinkingCat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TeaDrinkingCat" href="/user/show/4965293-teadrinkingcat">TeaDrinkingCat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236626063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6006894553046593700">Being a fan of animal fantasies, I decided to buy this quick read at my school book fair. Not worth the ten dollars. At least, not yet.<br/><br/>This book starts off fairly amazing, with creative ranks and how the Packs work. I did realize how large the writing font was, and it slightly worried me. But I'm used to reading short books, like Warriors.<br/>Anyway, the writer did seem to know what she was talking about. Being a wolf lover myself, I know tons of facts about these beautiful creatures. If I was about</span>
  <span id="freeText6006894553046593700" style="display:none">Being a fan of animal fantasies, I decided to buy this quick read at my school book fair. Not worth the ten dollars. At least, not yet.<br /><br />This book starts off fairly amazing, with creative ranks and how the Packs work. I did realize how large the writing font was, and it slightly worried me. But I'm used to reading short books, like Warriors.<br />Anyway, the writer did seem to know what she was talking about. Being a wolf lover myself, I know tons of facts about these beautiful creatures. If I was about nine, I would love this book, as it seems to have a high vocabulary for its child-like length.<br /><br />Only when Faolan gets taken in by the bear did this book get questioned by me. First of all, a bear? Really? That's highly unrealistic. I doubt her milk would even keep the wolf pup alive, let alone the pup be willing to drink it. Then when the bear cried. Animals do not cry. Not emotionally. And the tears seemed to be repeated every two scenes. Then, what really got under my skin, was that Faolan was said to have green eyes. Green. Eyes. Wolves cannot ever have green eyes. How can someone writing an entire series about wolves, get eye-color wrong? <br /><br />Not only did the facts slowly get more incorrect, but the character Faolan is downright annoying. He sounds somewhat of a jerk, even in his early life stage.<br /><br />I'm not finished, but I doubt this book will get any better.<br /><br />*UPDATE<br /><br />I've gotten fairly far into it. Only about ten or twenty pages left. But I'm not finishing it. It's too awful.<br /><br />The author seems to have run out of descriptions near the end. She began to use the word "arthritic" about every other sentence when talking about some wolf named MacDuncan.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />Okay, so this book was awful. Normally, if someone has already written a series, and begin another, they don't really connect the two. That's why there are series; so you CAN connect the two. <br />It really upset me when the author dragged in those stupid owls. I thought, "hey, everyone can write a bad book. Maybe this would be better than those owls." Boy, was I wrong. Of course, the author installs the freaky birds into it.<br /><br />Just so much of this book was wrong. I mean, if a thirteen year old like myself can find a gross amount of large and small errors, why should this book even be selling? It was just downright bad. I didn't understand half of it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6006894553046593700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer446436673" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3451878013565021638">A student who is in my yearbook class was so excited when he saw my classroom library that he came bounding over to me the first week and asked me, "You have so many books! So you read a lot, right? Have you read Wolves of the Beyond?!" He was so excited. And how can a teacher kill a kid's excitement in 2 seconds? By answering, "No. I'm not sure what that is..." Well, he was so flabbergasted by my lack of knowledge that he brought me the book to read, pretty much commanding me to. And I have to </span>
  <span id="freeText3451878013565021638" style="display:none">A student who is in my yearbook class was so excited when he saw my classroom library that he came bounding over to me the first week and asked me, "You have so many books! So you read a lot, right? Have you read Wolves of the Beyond?!" He was so excited. And how can a teacher kill a kid's excitement in 2 seconds? By answering, "No. I'm not sure what that is..." Well, he was so flabbergasted by my lack of knowledge that he brought me the book to read, pretty much commanding me to. And I have to say, I am pretty glad he did. <br /><br />Lone Wolf is obviously the beginning of what is going to be a majorly epic animal fantasy series similar to Erin Hunter's books and Redwall. This series is a spin-off of Lasky's Ga'Hoole series yet I never found that not reading Ga'Hoole hindered the story in the least. Though it takes place in the same land as the other series, it is new characters and still includes description and a map to help with the setting. <br /><br />While reading, there were 3 things that really impressed me. 1st, like most fantasy animal fiction, I am always amazed by how an author can get into the head of animals. Lasky describes the animal instincts, aggression and emotions in such a beautiful way as if she can read their minds. 2nd, the world building in phenomenal. It amazes me when an author can build such a high fantasy world for their animals to live in. Finally, the immense plot development that is required to make these epic series and ones that intertwine like Wolves of the Beyond and Ga'Hoole astonish me even more. <br /><br />Mentor text for: Setting, Characterization, Plot Development, Descriptive, World Building (Mapping)<br /><br />Snatch of Text: "In the Cave Before Time, he had seen two constellations of wolves. One was the starry one on the rock ceiling. The other "constellation" was not stars but the hunting and traveling formation of wolves running together. In that formation he had sensed a common feeling, a spirit of fellowship. It made him fell all the more lonely. He had wanted to run with those wolves, to be part of that "constellation," ever since he had first seen the picture." (p. 145)</span>

<div id="review_323370642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323370642?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven R. McEvoy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven R. McEvoy" href="/user/show/9030709-steven-r-mcevoy">Steven R. McEvoy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9030709-steven-r-mcevoy?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323370642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10328497811330543446">This story was amazing! It reads like a cross between The Jungle Book by Rudyard Kipling and A Wolf Story by James Byron Huggins, both of which I love and have reread many times. The story is powerful and compelling. It is the first book set in the world of Ga'Hoole that does not focus primarily on the Owl kingdoms. It was wonderful to read, and I immediately started book two after finishing book one. I could not wait until I had even written my review. I had to know what happened next.<br/><br/>It is the</span>
  <span id="freeText10328497811330543446" style="display:none">This story was amazing! It reads like a cross between The Jungle Book by Rudyard Kipling and A Wolf Story by James Byron Huggins, both of which I love and have reread many times. The story is powerful and compelling. It is the first book set in the world of Ga'Hoole that does not focus primarily on the Owl kingdoms. It was wonderful to read, and I immediately started book two after finishing book one. I could not wait until I had even written my review. I had to know what happened next.<br /><br />It is the story of Faolan, a young wolf who is left to die because of a birth defect. He ends up on an ice floe in a river during the spring thaw. He is plucked from the river by a she-bear, who has just lost her cub to a cougar. The bear decides to raise him. Over time he comes to realize he is different. He grows and learns from his second milk-mother Thunderheart. She realizes she will go to the long sleep and tries to prepare Faolan. But life is not always fair and much befalls Faolan during the winter. Soon he is in search of the Wolves of the Beyond.<br /><br />You cannot help but fall in love with the characters in the book. My only complaint is the covers are a little too 'Disney' for the actual content of the books. It looks like it will be the beginning of an amazing trilogy. I highly recommend them!<br /><br />Read the rest of the review and with links to other reviews of books by the author on my blog <a href="http://bit.ly/LoneWolfKL" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Reviews and More</a>. And also an author profile and interview with Kathryn Lasky.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10328497811330543446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4628570502153349003">Born with a splayed paw with an odd spiral design on the pad, Faolan is left to die. But Fate intervenes and the moments old wolf pup is quickly adopted by a heartbroken grizzly bear, affectionately named Thunderheart. Lone Wolf is the story of Faolan's first year of life.<br/><br/>I have not yet read the previous owl series by the same author, so I really had no idea what to expect. I was more than pleasantly surprised and am looking forward to sharing this book and the rest in the series with my son. <br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText4628570502153349003" style="display:none">Born with a splayed paw with an odd spiral design on the pad, Faolan is left to die. But Fate intervenes and the moments old wolf pup is quickly adopted by a heartbroken grizzly bear, affectionately named Thunderheart. Lone Wolf is the story of Faolan's first year of life.<br /><br />I have not yet read the previous owl series by the same author, so I really had no idea what to expect. I was more than pleasantly surprised and am looking forward to sharing this book and the rest in the series with my son. <br /><br />I was particularly moved by the depth of spirituality displayed in such a child-friendly manner, as well as the respect given to all living creatures. Lasky's hunting scenes are powerful and the respect afforded to the dying animal is a lesson to all humankind.<br /><br />Faolan's journey from abandoned pup, to adopted grizzly/wolf, to future pack member was heartening. Lessons were harsh, but not too harsh for young readers, and resulted in a maturing and intelligent young wolf destined for greatness and a compassionate heart.<br /><br />I only gave this 4 out of 5 stars because it ended much to aburptly, in a way that made it nearly impossible to not pick up the next book in the series (as well as now needing to get out and pick up the owl series as well).<br /><br />Great quick, but insightful, read for adults. Even better read for kids.</span>

<div id="review_131647124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131647124" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/582895-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131647124?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/582895-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/582895-andrew?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/582895-andrew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/582895-andrew?shelf=animals">animals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer131647124&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131647124" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17592175742992481089">This new series, set in the world of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole, can be read completely independently. (At least, this first book apparently can, because I've only read the first Ga'Hoole book, and didn't feel at all lost or spoiled.) It tells the tale of a young wolf with a splayed paw, cast out from the pack due to his deformity. He ends up being raised by a bear, and this mix of species helps illustrate the differences in animal behavior.<br/><br/>As with the Ga'Hoole book I've read, Lasky combines a co</span>
  <span id="freeText17592175742992481089" style="display:none">This new series, set in the world of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole, can be read completely independently. (At least, this first book apparently can, because I've only read the first Ga'Hoole book, and didn't feel at all lost or spoiled.) It tells the tale of a young wolf with a splayed paw, cast out from the pack due to his deformity. He ends up being raised by a bear, and this mix of species helps illustrate the differences in animal behavior.<br /><br />As with the Ga'Hoole book I've read, Lasky combines a compelling plot, an intricate fantasy mythology, and real animal behavior and psychology to create an exciting, fascinating read with three-dimensional characters. I'm glad to be in on (almost) the ground floor for this one, instead of having to catch up through fifteen already-published books. Reading this is a bit of an emotional roller coaster, because I'm such a sucker for animal stories. Can't wait to read the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17592175742992481089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2793002728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2793002728?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annette" href="/user/show/1426170-annette">Annette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1426170-annette?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1426170-annette?shelf=grace-reviewed">grace-reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2793002728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3960194884901662103">Review by Grace, age 8, 4/20/19<br/><br/>Floron was a wolf with a splayed paw. This means one of his paws has a spiral cut on it, and he was born like that. The wolves had rules that if any of the young pups have a splayed paw, twisted hip, no tail, or any kind of disease or disability they would be given to a special she-wolf called an "obra" who would set the pups down by the rushing river and leave them to - you know - die. <br/>The parents of those wolves would be set out of the tribe, never to breed again</span>
  <span id="freeText3960194884901662103" style="display:none">Review by Grace, age 8, 4/20/19<br /><br />Floron was a wolf with a splayed paw. This means one of his paws has a spiral cut on it, and he was born like that. The wolves had rules that if any of the young pups have a splayed paw, twisted hip, no tail, or any kind of disease or disability they would be given to a special she-wolf called an "obra" who would set the pups down by the rushing river and leave them to - you know - die. <br />The parents of those wolves would be set out of the tribe, never to breed again, so there would be no bad bloodlines in the clan. On the rare occasion when one of the pups with disabilities returns they would be placed on the lowest level of the wolves - a "gnaw" wolf. <br />Floron was found by a grizzly bear that he called "Thunder Heart." The bear took care of him, taught him to run faster than any wolf, and taught him to stand on his hind legs. But later that winter she had told him that he could go out and hunt things when she was asleep. But she woke up too early and forgot about Floron going. She died in an earthquake in late winter. <br />But Floron had found a pack to watch. There was one good "gnaw" wolf, but he was treated horribly and Floron did not want to be part of that clan. When he found another clan it seemed perfect, but his paw prints with the splayed paw left a mark that was like a foaming mouth disease. The wolves were forced to try to drive him into the fire. But he jumped over the fire and later that day he was got into that clan as a gnaw wolf because he had proved himself. <br />The rest of the story is about him surviving and hunting and hiding. <br />I liked this story because it's a survival story and I love those. I also like stories about animals that don't wear clothes and don't have humans. This is the only book I can compare to Wings of Fire! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3960194884901662103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_754619011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754619011" />
    <a title="Melinda Voong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24088455-melinda-voong"><img alt="Melinda Voong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379631708p2/24088455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754619011?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda Voong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda Voong" href="/user/show/24088455-melinda-voong">Melinda Voong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754619011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3849816917839134018">Personally, it wasn't that interesting to me. It doesn't have that much... Excitement, a hook to catch me on. I mean, the main thing I disliked though was the blandness of the main character.<br/><br/>The main character was too... How should I put this? Too overpowered. I get it's fictional, but this is based on survival and that kind of stuff, right? Then wolves should not be able to walk on two legs, be able to jump and pull down a cougar, and jump over a huge wall of fire. Like, seriously. If that isn'</span>
  <span id="freeText3849816917839134018" style="display:none">Personally, it wasn't that interesting to me. It doesn't have that much... Excitement, a hook to catch me on. I mean, the main thing I disliked though was the blandness of the main character.<br /><br />The main character was too... How should I put this? Too overpowered. I get it's fictional, but this is based on survival and that kind of stuff, right? Then wolves should not be able to walk on two legs, be able to jump and pull down a cougar, and jump over a huge wall of fire. Like, seriously. If that isn't overpowered, I don't know what is. <br /><br />Not to mention when he joined the pack, he had a 'broader chest' than other wolves, can gnaw better than the other wolves already... It's just not too interesting with a character who could do everything. Like conflicts? Easily solved, problem done and gone.<br /><br />He killed a caribou and a cougar by himself too. Let's see- The cougar could easily win. Let's face it, cougars are bigger and have stronger jaws. Faolan would not have won. The cougar wouldn't even have bolted, anyways. Especially if it knew it's enemy was one single wolf. And then the caribou. Wolves work in pack to bring down caribou. A well-placed kick can even kill Faolan too. <br /><br />But nope. He's too strong. Gotta live through it.<br /><br />Plus we don't get to see much of his personality either. At first it was him learning survival instincts and then Thunderheart dies and everything is just boring. He kills stuff, eats stuff, goes and looks around a cave... We don't get to explore him much anyways. <br /><br />The thing that bugged me most about this was it's main character. I'm certainly not going to read the rest of the series- Especially if this is how the main character is and if he's going to remain that way. Characters who are far too strong aren't just my taste because apparently, conflicts can be easily overcome. <br /><br />Plus he's just your run-of-the-mill one special character out of all the others. Tch. Boring read, annoying main character.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3849816917839134018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_524462899" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524462899" />
    <a title="Shelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16898962-shelli"><img alt="Shelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529192483p2/16898962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524462899?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelli" href="/user/show/16898962-shelli">Shelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545093118" href="/book/show/10132848-lone-wolf">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524462899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8732367499485610774">I first discovered Lasky when I saw the stunning and emotional Guardians movie in theaters. The beautiful animation and the heartfelt story grabbed me and never let me go until the end.<br/><br/>Unfortunately when I picked up the book series Guardians of Ga'Hoole, I found myself disappointed. The story wasn't nearly as gripping at the plotline of the movie (which they changed quite a bit), and the characters felt flat and one-dimensional. I read the first three books of the series and no more.<br/><br/>Despite how </span>
  <span id="freeText8732367499485610774" style="display:none">I first discovered Lasky when I saw the stunning and emotional Guardians movie in theaters. The beautiful animation and the heartfelt story grabbed me and never let me go until the end.<br /><br />Unfortunately when I picked up the book series Guardians of Ga'Hoole, I found myself disappointed. The story wasn't nearly as gripping at the plotline of the movie (which they changed quite a bit), and the characters felt flat and one-dimensional. I read the first three books of the series and no more.<br /><br />Despite how I felt, I decided to pick up Lone Wolf and give Lasky another shot, since I love wolves a lot more than I love owls. But again I came away with a 'meh' feeling after reading this. I love the IDEA of this story. A wolf pup cast out of his pack, raised by a bear, then rejoining the pack with a new perspective! Wow! The back of the book sure makes me want to read it! But the actual story itself doesn't live up to the grand idea.<br /><br />I was particularly turned off by how negative the pack life shown, being full of unfair wolves who treat the lesser ones so poorly. How a wolf with Faolan's status would be expected to scrape his face in the dirt and grovel to every other wolf. I couldn't for the life of me understand how a character like Faolan, who grew up free and strong with a bear, would ever want to be a member of these packs. I'm not sure Lasky did a good job explaining this, other than the ambiguous "a wolf should be with other wolves." (Also I find it a little silly and confounding that these packs of wild wolves use human Scottish names for their clans like MacDuncan and MacAngus. What's the point of that?)<br /><br />It certainly wasn't a horrible book, and I think I'll give the next few books in the series a shot, if I can find them second hand. But sad to say, this series does not get a stellar review from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8732367499485610774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17085010323469670286">This book was pretty good for what it was. I am loathe to give it three stars because it was better than that, but four seems too much so we'll settle with 3.5. I didn't realize til I picked it up at a Goodwill, but apparently this book is a continuation of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole series of which I know next to nothing about. (Except owls. I knew it had to do with owls.) Anyway, I really liked the way the book started it, but the middle section was kind of meh. I'm always a fan of animals havi</span>
  <span id="freeText17085010323469670286" style="display:none">This book was pretty good for what it was. I am loathe to give it three stars because it was better than that, but four seems too much so we'll settle with 3.5. I didn't realize til I picked it up at a Goodwill, but apparently this book is a continuation of the Guardians of Ga'Hoole series of which I know next to nothing about. (Except owls. I knew it had to do with owls.) Anyway, I really liked the way the book started it, but the middle section was kind of meh. I'm always a fan of animals having cultures and whatnot, but it got a little dense toward the middle. I think it was trying to connect things back to the original series? While you don't necessarily <i>have</i> to read the Guardians of Ga'Hoole to read this, I feel like it helps. Even as an adult I was a little overwhelmed and confused by the Cave Beyond Time. (It seemed kind of random to me that Faolan encountered it.) The plot however is somewhat intriguing and I'm curious as to what the swirl means. I probably will not actively be pursuing the other books in this series however.<br /><br />ETA: The one thing that did really annoy me is when the author talked several times about the wolves "Dropping to their knees" or "Pulling their knees to their chest." or something like that. Wolf knees don't work the same way as human knees. So a wolf dropping to his or her knees gives a weird, jarring mental image.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984908028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12181469521696025975">Lone Wolf by Kathryn Lasky tells the beginning of an abandoned wolf who is taken in by a bear who cares for him in his young age. The main and lone character, Faolan is nursed by Thunderheart, a lone female bear who is prepping for winter. The story leads with a heart warming tone, but some subtle events and actions eventually progress the story into a suspenseful and gruesome story of a lone wolf in a cruel world. <br/>The story does a good job in providing more and more questions for the main chara</span>
  <span id="freeText12181469521696025975" style="display:none">Lone Wolf by Kathryn Lasky tells the beginning of an abandoned wolf who is taken in by a bear who cares for him in his young age. The main and lone character, Faolan is nursed by Thunderheart, a lone female bear who is prepping for winter. The story leads with a heart warming tone, but some subtle events and actions eventually progress the story into a suspenseful and gruesome story of a lone wolf in a cruel world. <br />The story does a good job in providing more and more questions for the main character that are shared among the reader, which ads to a welcome element of mystery. At first, I had little interest in the book, despite reading the introduction some time ago. My disinterest was quickly diminished as tensions and unanswered oddities appear less than halfway through. <br />I'd recommend this to anyone who has enjoyed Lasky's other works or simply wants something new as the series is extensive and I plan to look into the second book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12181469521696025975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459538713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer900433770711353798">This is a book that will appeal to those who always want to cheer for the little guy and see him over come the obstacles they are faced with. The story is about a wolf pup who is abandoned do to his birth defect and has no one to turn to and left for dead. He is found by a mother bear who raises him the way she would raise her cub. Now the young wolf must adapt to his new way of life and find his own way when his mother is taken away from him and he truly becomes a loan wolf. It has a very descr</span>
  <span id="freeText900433770711353798" style="display:none">This is a book that will appeal to those who always want to cheer for the little guy and see him over come the obstacles they are faced with. The story is about a wolf pup who is abandoned do to his birth defect and has no one to turn to and left for dead. He is found by a mother bear who raises him the way she would raise her cub. Now the young wolf must adapt to his new way of life and find his own way when his mother is taken away from him and he truly becomes a loan wolf. It has a very descriptive appeal that can make you feel like you apart of the action. This book also connects to the other books written by Kathryn Lasky such as the Gaurdian of Gahol. This book has many challenges and plot build ups that will keep you wanting more.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zOQb1VAS46cNLOubkBbWmx7kEtDicZXPtu+9NF3OPbbJ0UmUPda8VZLbqXjHt+CUk5IMsyRdgwxcbkx17v9KTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fF3mmm/WzjcxnYvsjbN37vp+8zasibgMFsBkoSMzcL15aLTbAhKRxa5qyQ/aEkHhdwjtVWqlrs/8QZXgkAIHRQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9143025322414121322"><i>Kathryn Lasky</i> is the American author of many critically acclaimed books, including several Dear America books, several Royal Diaries books, 1984 Newbery Honor winning <i>Sugaring Time, The Night Journey</i>, and the <i>Guardians of Ga'Hoole</i> series.<br/><br/>She was born June 24, 1944, and grew up in Indianapolis, Indiana, and is married to Christopher Knight, with whom she lives in Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Book 15,<i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3301645.The_War_of_the_Ember' title='The War of the Ember' rel='nofollow noopener'>The War of t</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText9143025322414121322" style="display:none"><i>Kathryn Lasky</i> is the American author of many critically acclaimed books, including several Dear America books, several Royal Diaries books, 1984 Newbery Honor winning <i>Sugaring Time, The Night Journey</i>, and the <i>Guardians of Ga'Hoole</i> series.<br /><br />She was born June 24, 1944, and grew up in Indianapolis, Indiana, and is married to Christopher Knight, with whom she lives in Massachusetts.<br /><br />Book 15,<i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3301645.The_War_of_the_Ember" title="The War of the Ember" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Ember</a></i>, is currently the last book in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40440-guardians-of-ga-hoole" rel="nofollow noopener">Ga'Hoole series</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17166341.The_Rise_of_a_Legend" title="The Rise of a Legend" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rise of a Legend</a> is the 16th book but is a prequel to the series. Lasky has also written <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/774337.Guide_Book_To_The_Great_Tree" title="Guide Book To The Great Tree" rel="nofollow noopener">Guide Book To The Great Tree</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7209860.Lost_Tales_Of_Ga_Hoole" title="Lost Tales Of Ga'Hoole" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost Tales Of Ga'Hoole</a> which are companion books.</span>
